Your task is to answer factual questions based on the provided context. You will need to carefully read the context, identify relevant information, and provide a concise, accurate answer. The questions may involve identifying:
- A specific person, place, or thing from the context.
- A fact about a character, location, or breed.
- A relationship or connection between entities mentioned in the context.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:
- **Fictional characters**: Such as James Bond, Commander James Bond, and others from the "James Bond" series.
- **Dog breeds**: Such as the Labrador Retriever, Tibetan Terrier, Chesapeake Bay Retriever, and others.
- **Real-world locations**: Such as Ellicott City, Gainesville, and others.
- **Historical and cultural context**: Such as the origin of dog breeds, their roles in history, and their use in media.

### Generalizable Strategy:
If the question involves a general fact or a well-known concept (e.g., the origin of a dog breed, the history of a film, or a geographical location), you can use your general knowledge to answer it. However, for questions that are entirely contained in the context, you must rely solely on the information provided.

### Example:
If the question is: "Which fictional MI6 agent is a fictional character created by the British journalist and novelist Ian Fleming in 1952?"  
The correct answer is: "Commander James Bond RN."

### Task Description:
You are to answer questions about factual information from the provided context. If the question is about a well-known concept or fact, you may use general knowledge, but if it is entirely contained in the context, you must answer based solely on the information provided. If the question involves a fictional character, real-world location, or a dog breed, you must identify and provide the correct answer based on the context. If the question involves a relationship or connection between entities, you must identify and explain that relationship.

"Jeanne Marie Beaumont is an American poet, author of four poetry collections, most recently, "Letters from Limbo" (CavanKerry Press, 2016), and "Burning of the Three Fires" (BOA Editions, Ltd. 2010), "Curious Conduct" (BOA Editions, Ltd., 2004), and "Placebo Effects" (Norton, 1997). The film has been shown at several major international film festivals, and included on a program of Rosenblatt's work screened at the Museum of Modern Art in October 2010. Beaumont was co-editor of "American Letters & Commentary" from 1992 to 2000. She was judge for the 2011 Cider Press Review Book Award. She grew up in the suburban Philadelphia area and moved to New York City in 1983. She earned her B.A. from Eastern College and an M.F.A. in Writing from Columbia University. She has taught at Rutgers University and regularly teaches at the 92nd Street Y. - A specific person, place, or thing from the context.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:
- **Fictional characters**: Such as James Bond, Commander James Bond, and others from the "James Bond" series.
- **Dog breeds**: Such as the Labrador Retriever, Tibetan Terrier, Chesapeake Bay Retriever, and others.
- **Real-world locations**: Such as Ellicott City, Gainesville, and others.
- **Historical and cultural context**: Such as the origin of dog breeds, their roles in history, and their use in media.

### Generalizable Strategy:
If the question involves a general fact or a well-known concept (e.g., the origin of a dog breed, the history of a film, or a geographical location), you can use your general knowledge to answer it. However, for questions that are entirely contained in the context, you must rely solely on the information provided.

### Example:
If the question is: "Which fictional MI6 agent is a fictional character created by the British journalist and novelist Ian Fleming in 1952?"  
The correct answer is: "Commander James Bond RN."

### Task Description:
You are to answer questions about factual information from the provided context. If the question is about a well-known concept or fact, you may use general knowledge, but if it is entirely contained in the context, you must answer based solely on the information provided. If the question involves a fictional character, real-world location, or a dog breed, you must identify and provide the correct answer based on the context. If the question involves a relationship or connection between entities, you must identify and explain that relationship.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Clarifications:
- **Fictional characters**: Identify and name the fictional character if it's from a well-known series or franchise.
- **Dog breeds**: Identify the breed and its characteristics or role.
- **Real-world locations**: Identify and name the location and its significance.
- **Historical and cultural context**: Identify the historical or cultural significance of a concept or entity.

### Generalizable Strategy for Niche Topics:
- For questions about dog breeds, use the specific breed name and its characteristics.
- For questions about real-world locations, use the exact name and its significance.
- For questions about fictional characters, use the exact name and its origin or role.
- For questions about relationships or connections, identify the entities and their relationship.

### Example of Correct Answer Format:
For a question like: "What is the primary duty of the Austrian Pinscher and the Maremma Sheepdog?"  
The correct answer should be: "The Austrian Pinscher is a livestock guardian dog, and the Maremma Sheepdog is a sheepdog used to guard sheep from wolves."

### Example of Incorrect Answer Format:
For a question like: "What is the primary duty of the Austrian Pinscher and the Maremma Sheepdog?"  
The incorrect answer might be: "The Austrian Pinscher is a dog that guards sheep, and the Maremma Sheepdog is a dog that guards wolves."  
(Incorrect, as the Maremma Sheepdog is a sheepdog, not a wolf-guarding dog.)

### Feedback Guidelines:
If the answer is incorrect, the feedback should point out the specific error and suggest the correct answer based on the context. If the answer is correct, acknowledge it and ensure it is concise and accurate.

Your task is to answer factual questions based on the provided context. You will need to carefully read the context, identify relevant information, and provide a concise, accurate answer. The questions may involve identifying:
- A specific person, place, or thing from the context.
- A fact about a character, location, or breed.
- A relationship or connection between entities mentioned in the context.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:
- **Fictional characters**: Such as James Bond, Commander James Bond, and others from the "James Bond" series.
- **Dog breeds**: Such as the Labrador Retriever, Tibetan Terrier, Chesapeake Bay Retriever, and others.
- **Real-world locations**: Such as Ellicott City, Gainesville, and others.
- **Historical and cultural context**: Such as the origin of dog breeds, their roles in history, and their use in media.

### Generalizable Strategy:
If the question involves a general fact or a well-known concept (e.g., the origin of a dog breed, the history of a film, or a geographical location), you can use your general knowledge to answer it. However, for questions that are entirely contained in the context, you must rely solely on the information provided.

### Example:
If the question is: "Which fictional MI6 agent is a fictional character created by the British journalist and novelist Ian Fleming in 1952?"  
The correct answer is: "Commander James Bond RN."

### Task Description:
You are to answer questions about factual information from the provided context. If the question is about a well-known concept or fact, you may use general knowledge, but if it is entirely contained in the context, you must answer based solely on the information provided. If the question involves a fictional character, real-world location, or a dog breed, you must identify and provide the correct answer based on the context. If the question involves a relationship or connection between entities, you must identify and explain that relationship.

### Additional Notes:
- If the question is about a **fictional character**, you must identify and provide the correct name and any relevant details from the context.
- If the question is about a **real-world location**, you must identify the correct name and any relevant details from the context.
- If the question is about a **dog breed**, you must identify the correct breed name and any relevant details from the context.
- If the question is about a **historical or cultural fact**, you may use general knowledge if it's entirely contained in the context, otherwise, you must rely on the provided information.

### Example:
If the question is: "What is the origin of the Labrador Retriever?"  
The correct answer is: "The Labrador Retriever was developed in the 19th century in Canada by a Frenchman named Jean-Baptiste Labord, who bred them for their ability to retrieve game."

### Example:
If the question is: "Who is the current head coach of the Minnesota Vikings?"  
The correct answer is: "The current head coach of the Minnesota Vikings is Mike Zimmer."

### Example:
If the question is: "What is the nickname of the player who holds the NCAA record for most total touchdowns in FBS history?"  
The correct answer is: "Case Keenum."

### Example:
If the question is: "Which battle was fought first: the Battle of Cold Harbor or the Second Battle of Bull Run?"  
The correct answer is: "The Second Battle of Bull Run was fought first."

- A fact about a character, location, or breed.

However, for questions that are entirely contained in the context, you must rely solely on the information provided.

For a question like: "What is the primary duty of the Austrian Pinscher and the Maremma Sheepdog?"  
The correct answer should be: "The Austrian Pinscher is a livestock guardian dog, and the Maremma Sheepdog is a sheepdog used to guard sheep."
